        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  This work presents an up-to-date information on Na-based battery materials.  On the one hand, it explores the feasibility of two novel energy storage systems: Na-aq. batteries and Na-O2 technol.  On the other hand, it summarizes new advances on non-aq. Na-ion systems.  Although all of them can be placed under the umbrella of Na-based systems, aq. and oxygen-based batteries are arising technologies with increasing significance in energy storage research, while non-aq. sodium-ion technol. has become one of the most important research lines in this field.  These systems meet different requirements of energy storage: Na-aq. batteries will have a detg. role as a low cost and safer technol.; Na-O2 systems can be the key technol. to overcome the need for high energy d. storage devices; and non-aq. Na-ion batteries have application in the field of stationary energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqoMIYpy9lmPbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li5wvYcRakdFg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFOisr%252FF&amp;md5=2cb5179714ac258186fecdd5b6c69452</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1021/cr500192f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yabuuchi, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kubota, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dahbi, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Komaba, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Research Development on Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon-coated rutile titanium dioxide derived from titanium-metal organic framework with enhanced sodium storage behavior</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zou, Guoqiang; Chen, Jun; Zhang, Yan; Wang, Chao; Huang, Zhaodong; Li, Simin; Liao, Hanxiao; Wang, Jufeng; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">325</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">25-34</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon-coated rutile titanium dioxide (CRT) was fabricated through an in-situ pyrolysis of titanium-based metal org. framework (Ti8O8(OH)4[O2CC6H4CO2]6) crystals.  Benefiting from the Ti-O-C skeleton structure of titanium-based metal org. framework, the CRT possesses abundant channels and micro/mesopores with the diams. ranging from 1.06 to 4.14 nm, shows larger sp. surface area (245 m2 g-1) and better electronic cond. compared with pure titanium dioxide (12.8 m2 g-1).  When applied as anode material for sodium-ion batteries, the CRT electrode exhibits a high cycling performance with a reversible capacity of ∼175 mAh g-1 at 0.5 C-rate after 200 cycles, and obtains an excellent rate capability of ∼70 mAh g-1 after 2000 cycles even at a specific current of 3360 mA g-1(20 C-rate).  The outstanding rate capability can be attributed to the carbon-coated structure, which may effectively prevent aggregation of the titanium dioxide nanoparticles, accelerate the mass transfer of Na+ and speed up the charge transfer rate.  Considering these advantages of this particular framework structure, the CRT can serve as an alternative anode material for the industrial application of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoDlA3Cz55SObVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhyz17LXl_AuA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xpsl2jtL0%253D&amp;md5=82c2ae3f7ed54a4e80adb2f74f9c4976</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1039/c2ee02781j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Palomares, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Serras, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Villaluenga, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hueso, K.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-ion batteries, recent advances and present challenges to become low cost energy storage systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Palomares, Veronica; Serras, Paula; Villaluenga, Irune; Hueso, Karina B.; Carretero-Gonzalez, Javier; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5884-5901</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRYtxfVVW_sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhyz17LXl_AuA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XivFWnu7s%253D&amp;md5=72869139086b8ee9adec746418ff84b1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1149/1.3607983"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chevrier, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ceder, G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Challenges for Na-Ion Negative Electrodes</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have been proposed as candidates for replacing Li-ion batteries.  The authors examine the viability of Na-ion anode materials based on Na alloys or hard carbons in terms of volumetric energy d.  Due to the bigger size of the Na atom compared to the Li atom, Na alloys would lead to anode materials with about half the volumetric energy d. of their Li analogs.  Volumetric energy densities obtainable with sodiated hard carbons would also be significantly less than those obtainable with lithiated graphite.  These findings highlight the need of novel ideas for Na-ion anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpfbyHmIC7uUrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhyz17LXl_AuA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXpt1Ont7c%253D&amp;md5=f132981922c6ce146def4cd54c721e2b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.03.081"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Niu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pan, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, C.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">β-FeOOH: An Earth-Abundant High-Capacity Negative Electrode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Linghui; Wang, Luyuan Paul; Xi, Shibo; Yang, Ping; Du, Yonghua; Srinivasan, Madhavi; Xu, Zhichuan J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Thanks to the great earth abundance and excellent energy d. of Na, Na-ion batteries are promising alternative energy storage devices for large-scale applications.  Developing cheap, safe, and high-capacity Na-ion battery anode materials is one of the crit. challenges in this field.  Here, β-FeOOH is a very promising low-cost anode material, with a high reversible capacity (&gt;500 mA-h g-1 during initial cycles).  The fundamental characteristics assocd. with the discharge/charge processes, in terms of the redox reactions, formation/deformation of the solid electrolyte interface (SEI) layers, and structural and morphol. changes, are comprehensively studied.  A comparison study shows that the smaller-sized FeOOH has more serious kinetic restrictions, and thus lower capacities, while it shows better cyclability than the bigger one.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Intercalation of Sodium Ions into Hollow Iron Oxide Nanoparticles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Koo, Bonil; Chattopadhyay, Soma; Shibata, Tomohiro; Prakapenka, Vitali B.; Johnson, Christopher S.; Rajh, Tijana; Shevchenko, Elena V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">245-252</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Cation vacancies in hollow γ-Fe2O3 nanoparticles are utilized for efficient sodium ion transport.  As a result, fast rechargeable cathodes can be assembled from Earth-abundant elements such as iron oxide and sodium.  Structural and electronic transformations of hollow iron oxide nanoparticles are monitored in situ by synchrotron X-ray adsorption and diffraction techniques.  The results revealed that the cation vacancies in hollow γ-Fe2O3 nanoparticles can serve as hosts for sodium ions in high voltage range (4.0-1.1 V), allowing utilization of γ-Fe2O3 nanoparticles as a cathode material with high capacity (up to 189 mAh/g), excellent Coulombic efficiency (99.0%), good capacity retention, and superior rate performance (up to 99 mAh/g at 3000 mA/g (50 C)).  The appearance of the capacity at high voltage in iron oxide that is a typical anode and the fact that this capacity is comparable with the capacities obsd. in typical cathodes emphasize the importance of the proper understanding of the structure-properties correlation.  In addn. to that, encapsulation of hollow γ-Fe2O3 nanoparticles between two layers of carbon nanotubes allows fabrication of lightwt., binder-free, flexible, and stable electrodes.  The effect is discussed of electrolyte salts such as NaClO4 and NaPF6 on the Coulombic efficiency at different cycling rates.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqRLpCvmV6_rbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhSjY7w9-lk9A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhvVCqsrrM&amp;md5=a4748f0eb8d1deed81c19a7a17969851</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201303971"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, H.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Review.  A promising family of mixed transition-metal oxides (MTMOs) (designated as AxB3-xO4; A, B=Co, Ni, Zn, Mn, Fe, etc.) with stoichiometric or even non-stoichiometric compns., typically in a spinel structure, has recently attracted increasing research interest worldwide.  Benefiting from their remarkable electrochem. properties, these MTMOs will play significant roles for low-cost and environmentally friendly energy storage/conversion technologies.  In this Review, we summarize recent research advances in the rational design and efficient synthesis of MTMOs with controlled shapes, sizes, compns., and micro-/nanostructures, along with their applications as electrode materials for lithium-ion batteries and electrochem. capacitors, and efficient electrocatalysts for the oxygen redn. reaction in metal-air batteries and fuel cells.         </div><div class="casAbstract">NiCo2O4 is a potential lithium-ion battery (LIB) anode material that can be applied to the industrial prodn. for com. applications. Herein, graphene-based NiCo2O4 nanosheet arrays directly grown on nickel foam have been successfully synthesized.  This composites array shows significantly improved lithium storage properties with higher reversible capacity and better cycling stability than NiCo2O4 nanosheets.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High Electrochemical Performance of Monodisperse NiCo2O4 Mesoporous Microspheres as an Anode Material for Li-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Jingfa; Xiong, Shenglin; Liu, Yurong; Ju, Zhicheng; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">981-988</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Binary metal oxides have been regarded as ideal and potential anode materials, which can ameliorate and offset the electrochem. performance of the single metal oxides, such as reversible capacity, structural stability and electronic cond.  In this work, monodisperse NiCo2O4 mesoporous microspheres are fabricated by a facile solvothermal method followed by pyrolysis of the Ni0.33Co0.67CO3 precursor.  The Brunauer-Emmett-Teller surface area of NiCo2O4 mesoporous microspheres is detd. to be about 40.58 m2 g-1 with dominant pore diam. of 14.5 nm and narrow size distribution of 10-20 nm.  Our as-prepd. NiCo2O4 products were evaluated as the anode material for the lithium-ion battery application.  It is demonstrated that the special structural features of the NiCo2O4 microspheres including uniformity of the surface texture, the integrity and porosity exert significant effect on the electrochem. performances.  The discharge capacity of NiCo2O4 microspheres could reach 1198 mA h g-1 after 30 discharge-charge cycles at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1.  More importantly, when the c.d. increased to 800 mA·g-1, it can render reversible capacity of 705 mA h g-1 even after 500 cycles, indicating its potential applications for next-generation high power lithium-ion batteries.  The superior battery performance is mainly attributed to the unique micro/nanostructure composed of interconnected NiCo2O4 nanocrystals, which provides good electrolyte diffusion and large electrode-electrolyte contact area, and meanwhile reduces vol. change during charge/discharge process.  The strategy is simple but very effective, and because of its versatility, it could be extended to other high-capacity metal oxide anode materials for lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGozxBuRilGL2rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhmRM95rhMN5Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXoslOitg%253D%253D&amp;md5=2f1ae4ebb15717931c9b659dc9c906ba</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1021/cm025556v"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Alcántara, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jaraba, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lavela, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tirado, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NiCo<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub> Spinel: First Report on a Transition Metal Oxide for the Negative Electrode of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hybrid materials of graphene anchored with CoFe2O4 for the anode in sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Feng, Jian-Min; Zhong, Xia-Hua; Wang, Gui-Zhi; Dong, Lei; Li, Xi-Fei; Li, De-Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Science</span>

                        cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Exceptionally highly performing Na-ion battery anode using crystalline SnO2 nanoparticles confined in mesoporous carbon</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jahel, Ali; Ghimbeu, Camelia Matei; Darwiche, Ali; Vidal, Loic; Hajjar-Garreau, Samar; Vix-Guterl, Cathie; Monconduit, Laure</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11960-11969</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Confined and unconfined SnO2 nanoparticles in the pores of mesoporous carbon were prepd. and tested as anode materials vs. Na.  Both composites present small cryst. SnO2 particles (∼3 nm) but different location and dispersion in the carbon matrix.  When the particles are homogeneously distributed and confined in the carbon pores, an initial reversible capacity of 780 mA h g-1 is achieved with unprecedented capacity retention of 80 and 54% after 100 and 4000 cycles, resp., at a high current rate (50 C, 1800 mA g-1).  Unexpectedly, over two current rate variation cycles from 1 C to 500 C, the composite recovers 81% and 97%, resp. after returning from the 500 C to the 1 C rate.  To our knowledge, no other material with such a long cycling life and superior performance in terms of capacity and rate capability has been reported so far for sodium ion batteries.  HRTEM, XRD, N2 adsorption, XPS and galvanostatic cycling results suggest that confined SnO2 particles undergo an enhanced sodium alloying/dealloying process due to their special confinement inside the pores, which increases their cond., facilitates the diffusion of Na+ ions and buffers the large volumetric changes during charge/discharge.  These high performances cannot be delivered when SnO2 is not confined and not well dispersed in the carbon pores.  This work demonstrates that nano-confinement of anode species in carbon is a valuable concept affording the modification of the fundamental properties of guest species along with their electrochem. performances leading to highly stable and performing materials with a long life for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpmSgtWPTSt8LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0likZZPFSxpAYw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXnsFGgur4%253D&amp;md5=219ee2777f1e53956a82fdbab173128f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2012.01.123"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jin, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Composite of Sulfur and Polypyrrole-Multi Walled Carbon Combinatorial Nanotube as Cathode for Li/S Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A new high-performance cathode material for rechargeable lithium-ion batteries: Polypyrrole/vanadium oxide nanotubes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cui, Chao-Jun; Wu, Guang-Ming; Yang, Hui-Yu; She, Shi-Feng; Shen, Jun; Zhou, Bin; Zhang, Zhi-Hua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

                        cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrode materials with tailored facets for electrochemical energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Faxing; Wang, Xiaowei; Chang, Zheng; Zhu, Yusong; Fu, Lijun; Liu, Xiang; Wu, Yuping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale Horizons</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In recent years, the design and morphol. control of crystals with tailored facets have become hot spots in the field of electrochem. energy storage devices.  For electrode materials, morphologies play important roles in their activities because their shapes det. how many facets of specific orientation are exposed and therefore available for surface reactions.  This review focuses on the strategies for crystal facet control and the unusual electrochem. properties of electrode materials bound by tailored facets.  Here, electrode materials with tailored facets include transition metal oxides such as SnO2, Co3O4, NiO, Cu2O, and MnO2, elementary substances such as Si and Au, and intercalation compds. such as Li4Ti5O12, LiCoO2, LiMn2O4, LiFePO4, and Na0.7MnO2 for various applications of Li-ion batteries, aq. rechargeable lithium batteries, Na-ion batteries, Li-O2 batteries and supercapacitors.  How these electrode materials with tailored facets affect their electrochem. properties is discussed.  Finally, research opportunities as well as the challenges in this emerging research frontier are highlighted.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpnBkbw2Qn6CbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lghUZwpfw6Ivw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkvFCktw%253D%253D&amp;md5=b04efeb748b54942101659b45d042615</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1016/j.matlet.2014.07.170"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fan, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ma, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Miao, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In-Situ Synthesis of Core/Shell Structured Polypyrrole/Hydroquinone Nano-Beads and Electrochemical Capacitance Investigations</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Mater.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fe-Doped MnxOy with Hierarchical Porosity as a High-performance Lithium-ion Battery Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ma, Yue; Fang, Chunliu; Ding, Bo; Ji, Ge; Lee, Jim Yang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">33</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4646-4652</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We reported an alternative approach to designing and constructing 3-D manganese oxides with mixed-conducting properties.  Fe-doped MnxOy with connected macropores and mesopores to provide a hierarchical porosity was produced by a facile and scalable nanocasting technique followed by controlled calcination, using a novel macroporous amine-functionalized bromomethylated poly(2,6-dimethyl-1,4-phenylene oxide) (BPPO) membrane as the sacrificial template.  The macropores in the final product were mainly formed by the reverse-replication of the membrane porous structure, and interconnected via branches in the pore system.  The macropores cushioned the vol. change in the conversion reaction during cycling, and also acted as reservoirs and thoroughfares to improve Li+ transport in the electrolyte phase.  The mesopores between nanocryst. primary particles were formed upon heat treatment; and provided the large interfacial contact between electrolyte and electrode material to support a high Li+ flux across the solid/liq. interface.  The selection of iron as a dopant was intentional: The redox potential of iron (1.0 V for discharge/1.7 V for charge) is higher than that of manganese (0.5 V for discharge/1.2 V for charge).  Hence, the evenly distributed iron could remain in the zero valent state during a large part of MnxOy conversion reaction, serving conceptually the dual function of 1) elec. wiring of the electroactive material to lower the resistance to electron transport and 2) promoting ionic conduction by creating narrowly spaced interfaces at the oxide grain boundary.  Electrochem. measurements showed that the Fe-doped MnxOy composite had the best overall performance: a large reversible capacity of 620 mA.h.g-1 for 100 cycles at the c.d. of 200 mA.g-1, good rate capability up to 1600 mA.g-1 and outstanding cycle life even at very high c.d. (900 cycles at 1500 mA.g-1).  The cycle stability of the Fe-doped MnxOy composite suggests that it has the potential to be a candidate anode material for the next-generation Li ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp2UWqyK2x2vLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lghvEGnWnfqRQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtVSht73L&amp;md5=f186f7f53df3889a06ed12323eb6d531</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2009.10.039"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Novel Method for Preparing LiFePO<sub>4</sub> Nanorods as a Cathode Material for Lithium-Ion Power Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A Cu-Co alloy dendrite with a hierarchical nanostructure was electrochem. synthesized, and it characterized using scanning electron microscope, energy dispersive x-ray spectroscopy, time-of-flight secondary ion mass spectrometry (TOF-SIMS), X-ray diffractometry, XPS, coulometry, and cyclic voltammetry.  The catalytic characteristics of the dendrite were examd. for its use with highly sensitive glucose and H2O2 sensors.  The TOF-SIMS image shows that the Cu-Co alloy dendrite grew homogeneously in a hierarchical structure.  The Co2+ ions that formed on the alloy dendrite mainly contributed to glucose oxidn., and the Cu+ ion cooperated synergically with the Co2+ ion. The major oxidn. products of glucose on the dendrite is formate (12-electron oxidn. product) through coulometry and product anal. with a HPLC-MS analyzer.  The linear calibration plots for the glucose and H2O2 analyses were obtained between 0.5 μM to 14.0 mM (detection limit was 0.10 ± 0.05 μM) and 1.0 μM to 11.0 mM (detection limit was 0.75 ± 0.15 μM), resp.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Oxidation states of active catalytic centers in ethanol steam reforming reaction on ceria based Rh promoted Co catalysts: An XPS study</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Varga, Erika; Ferencz, Zsuzsa; Oszko, Albert; Erdohelyi, Andras; Kiss, Janos</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Molecular Catalysis A: Chemical</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">X-ray photoelectron spectroscopic (XPS) studies were carried out to study the oxidn. states of CeO2 and CeO2 supported Co-Rh catalysts during the temp. programmed stream reforming of EtOH reaction (SRE).                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cobalt sulfide/N,S codoped porous carbon core-shell nanocomposites as superior bifunctional electrocatalysts for oxygen reduction and evolution reactions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Binling; Li, Rong; Ma, Guiping; Gou, Xinglong; Zhu, Yanqiu; Xia, Yongde</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">48</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20674-20684</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Exploring highly-efficient and low-cost bifunctional electrocatalysts for both oxygen redn. reaction (ORR) and oxygen evolution reactions (OER) in the renewable energy area has gained momentum but still remains a significant challenge.  Here we present a simple but efficient method that utilizes ZIF-67 as the precursor and template for the one-step generation of homogeneous dispersed cobalt sulfide/N,S-codoped porous carbon nanocomposites as high-performance electrocatalysts.  Due to the favorable mol.-like structural features and uniform dispersed active sites in the precursor, the resulting nanocomposites, possessing a unique core-shell structure, high porosity, homogeneous dispersion of active components together with N and S-doping effects, not only show excellent electrocatalytic activity towards ORR with the high onset potential (around -0.04 V vs. -0.02 V for the benchmark Pt/C catalyst) and four-electron pathway and OER with a small overpotential of 0.47 V for 10 mA cm-2 c.d., but also exhibit superior stability (92%) to the com. Pt/C catalyst (74%) in ORR and promising OER stability (80%) with good methanol tolerance.  Our findings suggest that the transition metal sulfide-porous carbon nanocomposites derived from the one-step simultaneous sulfurization and carbonization of zeolitic imidazolate frameworks are excellent alternative bifunctional electrocatalysts towards ORR and OER in the next generation of energy storage and conversion technologies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqsUUZaspwot7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgElodGB0I-QQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVWmtLnJ&amp;md5=07464519b0c3a9d6177a22b0de1a83de</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1039/c3cy00192j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Laassiri, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bion, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Duprez, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Alamdari, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Royer, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Role of M<sup>n+</sup> Cations In the Redox and Oxygen Transfer Properties of BaM<sub>x</sub>Al<sub>12–x</sub>O<sub>19−δ</sub> (M= Mn, Fe, Co) Nanomaterials for High Temperature Methane Oxidation</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Catal.         </div><div class="casAbstract">BaMxAl12-xO19-δ (M = Mn, Fe, Co, x = 1, 2) hexaaluminate nanomaterials were successfully prepd. using the ARS (Activated Reactive Synthesis) process, a top-down and solvent free original synthesis route.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Co3O4 mesoporous nanosheets/three-dimensional graphene networks (Co3O4 MNSs/3DGNs) nanohybrids were successfully synthesized and investigated as anode materials for sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  Microstructure characterizations were performed to confirm the 3DGNs and Co3O4 MNSs nanostructures.  The present Co3O4 MNSs/3DGNs nanohybrids exhibit better SIB performance with enhanced reversible capacity, good cycle performance and rate capability as compared to Co3O4 MNSs and Co3O4 nanoparticles.  The improved electrochem. performance is considered due to the mesoporous nature of the products, the addn. of 3DGNs, 3D assembled hierarchical architecture and decrease in vol. expansion during cycling.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-dimensional NiCo2O4 nanowire arrays: preparation and storage behavior for flexible lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries with improved electrochemical performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mo, Yudi; Ru, Qiang; Chen, Junfen; Song, Xiong; Guo, Lingyun; Hu, Shejun; Peng, Shaomin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The growth of three-dimensional (3D) porous NiCo2O4 nanowire arrays on a carbon fiber cloth (denoted as NCO@CFC) via a facile low-cost soln. method combined with a subsequent annealing treatment is reported.  The structure and morphol. of the materials were characterized by X-ray diffraction, field-emission SEM, and transmission electron microscopy.  Owing to the unique 3D hierarchical architecture, the NCO@CFC nanowires as a flexible electrode material for lithium-ion batteries exhibit a stable cycling performance (92.3% retention after 100 cycles), a fairly high rate capacity (507 mA h/g at 4000 mA/g), and an enhanced lithium storage capacity.  When employed as an electrode material for sodium-ion batteries, the NCO@CFC is investigated in comparison with a 3D ordered array structure and exhibits similar charge/discharge characteristics and a feasible electrochem. performance.  The greatly improved electrochem. performance could be ascribed to the 3D porous nanostructure of the NCO@CFC nanowire arrays together with a novel carbon skeleton, which provides enough space to allow vol. expansion during the Li+/Na+ insertion/extn. process and facilitates rapid transport of ions and electrons.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoXw_-7XiLxqbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgElodGB0I-QQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrode materials for aqueous asymmetric supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Faxing; Xiao, Shiying; Hou, Yuyang; Hu, Chenglin; Liu, Lili; Wu, Yuping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  An asym. supercapacitor (ASC) is a supercapacitor based on two different electrode materials.  One electrode is based on redox (Faradic) reactions with or without non-faradaic reactions, and the other one is mostly based on elec. double-layer (non-Faradic or electrostatic) absorption/desportion.  Aq. electrolytes have higher ionic cond., larger capacitance and better safety than the org. electrolytes.  Herein, some key electrode materials for aq. ASCs are primarily reviewed, which provide a new direction for power sources to have higher energy d. at high power densities, compared with traditional capacitors.  Their neg. electrode materials include carbonaceous materials (porous carbons, carbon nanotubes and graphene), oxides (V2O5 and MoO3) and their composites, and their pos. electrode materials include carbonaceous materials, oxides (RuO2, MnO2, MoO3, V2O5, PbO2, Co3O4), Ni(OH)2, intercalation compds. (LiCoO2, LiMn2O4, Li[NiCoMn]1/3O2, NaMnO2 and KMnO2).  We describe the latest work on these electrode materials, and a particular focus is directed to the fabrication and electrochem. performance of various nanostructured electrode materials and some assembled ASCs.  Finally, the future trends and prospects on advanced energy storage materials are suggested.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpQJfcktMTcw7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgElodGB0I-QQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFeqtr3O&amp;md5=512cd93a2cde72e85beda226e109d32b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA01398H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Conductive Polymer Coated MoO<sub>3</sub> Anode Enables an Al-Ion Capacitor with High Performance</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A conductive polymer coated MoO3 anode enables an Al-ion capacitor with high performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Faxing; Liu, Zaichun; Wang, Xiaowei; Yuan, Xinhai; Wu, Xiongwei; Zhu, Yusong; Fu, Lijun; Wu, Yuping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5115-5123</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. capacitors are becoming promising energy conversion/storage and power output devices.  However, high cost and low energy d. are two serious disadvantages.  By integrating the advantages of Li-/Na-ion batteries and electrochem. capacitors, Li-/Na-ion capacitors have been explored recently.  Al is very cheap and is the most abundant metal element on the earth.  There are few reports on Al-ion capacitors due to the challenges in finding a suitable anode with large capacitance and good rate performance.  Here, the feasibility of assembling an Al-ion capacitor with good electrochem. performance is demonstrated.  The Al-ion capacitor is assembled by using a composite of MoO3 nanotubes coated by a conductive polypyrrole (PPy@MoO3) as an anode, which functions via a redox intercalation/deintercalation of Al3+ ions in aq. soln.  It delivers a capacitance of 693 F/g, about 3 times higher than that of electrode materials for sodium-ion capacitors in aq. soln.  Combined with an activated carbon (AC) cathode, the Al-ion capacitor presents an energy d. of 30 W h/kg and an excellent cycling life with 93% capacitance retention after 1800 cycles.  This finding provides another energy storage device with low cost and promotes the application of capacitors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr-B8WDSiffkbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhlG20W3f0X4w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XjsVGlsLw%253D&amp;md5=7c98fb2f66d51d6f363b28d504efb300</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2012.09.100"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Holze, R.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polypyrrole-Coated LiV<sub>3</sub>O<sub>8</sub>-Nanocomposites with Good Electrochemical Performance as Anode Material for Aqueous Rechargeable Lithium Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Aging of Co(Ni)MoP/Al2O3 catalysts in working state</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guichard, B.; Roy-Auberger, M.; Devers, E.; Legens, C.; Raybaud, P.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Catalysis Today</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The deactivation behavior of Co(Ni)MoP/Al2O3 catalysts during diesel fuel hydrotreatment is investigated by means of XPS and transmission electron microscopy (TEM).  XPS measurements performed on aged Co(Ni)MoP/Al2O3 catalysts show that the promoter quantity on the edges of MoS2 nano-crystallites decreases with increasing lifetime.  TEM coupled with energy dispersive X-ray spectrometry (EDX) indicates that the Co(Ni)/Mo ratio inside crystallites changes without any modification over MoS2 layers (size and stacking).  Moreover toluene hydrogenation activity loss on aged catalysts is found to be linearly correlated to the XPS promotion rate decrease during deactivation.  These exptl. results have been analyzed in the light of recent d. functional theory (DFT) calcns. on the thermodn. stability of Co(Ni)MoS phases in sulfo-reductive working conditions.  It is shown that the destabilization of the mixed phase may be partially attributed to the reaction conditions (high temp. and reductive environment).  In addn., the role of the coke cannot be excluded to explain the promotion rate decrease revealed by XPS spectra.  The exptl. results combined with DFT results are used to propose an origin of the active phase modifications in working state.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGonhMrfX-0PnLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhlG20W3f0X4w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2sXhtlKrtrrL&amp;md5=881521f28a428d2a0cda4f91575f4ec6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.01.214"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huo, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dai, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A High Performance Cobalt Sulfide Counter Electrode for Dye-Sensitized Solar Cells</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Modifying magnetic properties of ultrathin magnetite films by growth on Fe pre-covered MgO(001)</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Schemme, T.; Krampf, A.; Bertram, F.; Kuschel, T.; Kuepper, K.; Wollschlaeger, J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Applied Physics (Melville, NY, United States)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Fe oxide films were reactively grown on Fe buffer films, which were deposited before on MgO(001) substrates to analyze the influence of the initial Fe buffer layers on the magnetic properties of the magnetite films.  XPS and LEED showed that magnetite films of high cryst. quality in the surface near region were formed by this two-step deposition procedure.  The underlying Fe film, however, was completely oxidized as proved by x-ray reflectometry and diffraction.  The structural bulk quality of the Fe oxide film is poor compared to magnetite films directly grown on MgO(001).  Although the Fe film was completely oxidized, the authors found drastically modified magnetic properties for these films using the magnetooptic Kerr effect.  The magnetite films had strongly increased coercive fields, and their magnetic in-plane anisotropy is in-plane rotated by 45° compared to magnetite films formed directly by one step reactive growth on MgO(001).                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Investigation of multiplet splitting of Fe 2p XPS spectra and bonding in iron compounds</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Grosvenor, A.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Ferrous (Fe2+) and ferric (Fe3+) compds. were studied by XPS to det. the usefulness of calcd. multiplet peaks to fit high-resoln. Fe 2p3/2 spectra from high-spin compds.  The multiplets fit most spectra well, particularly when contributions attributed to surface peaks and shake-up satellites were included.  This information was useful for fitting of the complex Fe 2p3/2 spectra for Fe3O4 where both Fe2+ and Fe3+ species are present.  As the ionic bond character of the Fe-ligand bond increased, the binding energy assocd. with either the ferrous or ferric 2p3/2 photoelectron peak increased.  This is due to the decrease in shielding of the Fe cation by the more increasingly electroneg. ligands.  Also the difference in energy between a high-spin Fe 2p3/2 peak and its corresponding shake-up satellite peak increased as the electronegativity of the ligand increased.  The extrinsic loss spectra for Fe oxides are reported; these are as characteristic of each species as are the photoelectron peaks.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqII9QNo6oMwLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhUWxTsJp1XWA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD2MXjtVWgtQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=c71a7fc95f7cc23cc7b2de08dfb3b5c6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA06708H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tan, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chou, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dou, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">One-Pot Synthesis of Ultra-Small Magnetite Nanoparticles on the Surface of Reduced Graphene Oxide Nanosheets as Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Their morphol., structure and electrochem. performance were characterized by field emission SEM, transmission electron microscopy, X-ray diffraction, nitrogen adsorption-desorption isotherms, galvanostatic charge/discharge tests, cyclic voltammetry and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy, resp.  The results show that MFO/RGO composite with 20 wt.% RGO exhibits a max. reversible capacity of about 347.5 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 after 70 cycles with good cycling stability.  The excellent electrochem. performance of MFO/RGO composites should be attributed to the synergistic effect of MFO and RGO to form a porous conductive network structure which offers the increased sp. surface area, the facilitated electron transfer ability and the effective buffering of vol. expansion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr_dCg6DUiuhLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljShv46DNTCmw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVyjur3O&amp;md5=cb73bb0af3e1223d28e31908bb466d0e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref55'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit55" data-doi="10.1021/am400497v"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Teh, P. Although all of them can be placed under the umbrella of Na-based systems, aq. and oxygen-based batteries are arising technologies with increasing significance in energy storage research, while non-aq. sodium-ion technol. has become one of the most important research lines in this field.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Cube-shaped porous C (CPC) was obtained from the carbonization of MOF-5 (Zn4O(OOCC6H4COO)3) crystals and shows abundant micro/mesopores, high mech. strength, largest surface area (2316 m2 g-1, BET method) and good elec. cond. (a high wt. ratio 98.17/1.83 of C/O).  When used as anode material for Na-ion batteries, the CPC presents a high overall Na storage capacity ∼240 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles, and maintains a high specific capacity of 100 mAh g-1 after 5000 cycles at a c.d. of 3200 mA g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbon-coated rutile titanium dioxide (CRT) was fabricated through an in-situ pyrolysis of titanium-based metal org. framework (Ti8O8(OH)4[O2CC6H4CO2]6) crystals.  Benefiting from the Ti-O-C skeleton structure of titanium-based metal org. framework, the CRT possesses abundant channels and micro/mesopores with the diams. ranging from 1.06 to 4.14 nm, shows larger sp. surface area (245 m2 g-1) and better electronic cond. compared with pure titanium dioxide (12.8 m2 g-1).  When applied as anode material for sodium-ion batteries, the CRT electrode exhibits a high cycling performance with a reversible capacity of ∼175 mAh g-1 at 0.5 C-rate after 200 cycles, and obtains an excellent rate capability of ∼70 mAh g-1 after 2000 cycles even at a specific current of 3360 mA g-1(20 C-rate).  The outstanding rate capability can be attributed to the carbon-coated structure, which may effectively prevent aggregation of the titanium dioxide nanoparticles, accelerate the mass transfer of Na+ and speed up the charge transfer rate.  Considering these advantages of this particular framework structure, the CRT can serve as an alternative anode material for the industrial application of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoDlA3Cz55SObVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgE22CNUWHZWw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xpsl2jtL0%253D&amp;md5=82c2ae3f7ed54a4e80adb2f74f9c4976</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref8" class="rightTabRefNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit8" data-doi="10.1039/c2ee02781j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Palomares, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Serras, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Villaluenga, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hueso, K.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRYtxfVVW_sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgE22CNUWHZWw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XivFWnu7s%253D&amp;md5=72869139086b8ee9adec746418ff84b1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref9" class="rightTabRefNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit9" data-doi="10.1149/1.3607983"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chevrier, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ceder, G.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Challenges for Na-Ion Negative Electrodes</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. The authors examine the viability of Na-ion anode materials based on Na alloys or hard carbons in terms of volumetric energy d.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Thanks to the great earth abundance and excellent energy d. of Na, Na-ion batteries are promising alternative energy storage devices for large-scale applications.  Developing cheap, safe, and high-capacity Na-ion battery anode materials is one of the crit. challenges in this field.  Here, β-FeOOH is a very promising low-cost anode material, with a high reversible capacity (&gt;500 mA-h g-1 during initial cycles).  The fundamental characteristics assocd. with the discharge/charge processes, in terms of the redox reactions, formation/deformation of the solid electrolyte interface (SEI) layers, and structural and morphol. changes, are comprehensively studied.  A comparison study shows that the smaller-sized FeOOH has more serious kinetic restrictions, and thus lower capacities, while it shows better cyclability than the bigger one.  Origins of the large overpotential are discussed, and probably the overpotential should be mainly due to the features of the surface-concn.-dependent potential and the slow diffusion of Na+; the presence of the SEI layers may also contribute to the overpotential.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoNxxDSrqiql7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj6WBEH75i-yg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFyru7bJ&amp;md5=11c684347db719160d0abe09a2211d8d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1021/cm303611z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Koo, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chattopadhyay, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shibata, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Prakapenka, V.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Cation vacancies in hollow γ-Fe2O3 nanoparticles are utilized for efficient sodium ion transport.  As a result, fast rechargeable cathodes can be assembled from Earth-abundant elements such as iron oxide and sodium.  Structural and electronic transformations of hollow iron oxide nanoparticles are monitored in situ by synchrotron X-ray adsorption and diffraction techniques.  The results revealed that the cation vacancies in hollow γ-Fe2O3 nanoparticles can serve as hosts for sodium ions in high voltage range (4.0-1.1 V), allowing utilization of γ-Fe2O3 nanoparticles as a cathode material with high capacity (up to 189 mAh/g), excellent Coulombic efficiency (99.0%), good capacity retention, and superior rate performance (up to 99 mAh/g at 3000 mA/g (50 C)).  The appearance of the capacity at high voltage in iron oxide that is a typical anode and the fact that this capacity is comparable with the capacities obsd. in typical cathodes emphasize the importance of the proper understanding of the structure-properties correlation.  In addn. to that, encapsulation of hollow γ-Fe2O3 nanoparticles between two layers of carbon nanotubes allows fabrication of lightwt., binder-free, flexible, and stable electrodes.  The effect is discussed of electrolyte salts such as NaClO4 and NaPF6 on the Coulombic efficiency at different cycling rates.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqRLpCvmV6_rbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj6WBEH75i-yg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhvVCqsrrM&amp;md5=a4748f0eb8d1deed81c19a7a17969851</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201303971"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, H.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Review.  A promising family of mixed transition-metal oxides (MTMOs) (designated as AxB3-xO4; A, B=Co, Ni, Zn, Mn, Fe, etc.) with stoichiometric or even non-stoichiometric compns., typically in a spinel structure, has recently attracted increasing research interest worldwide.  Benefiting from their remarkable electrochem. properties, these MTMOs will play significant roles for low-cost and environmentally friendly energy storage/conversion technologies.  In this Review, we summarize recent research advances in the rational design and efficient synthesis of MTMOs with controlled shapes, sizes, compns., and micro-/nanostructures, along with their applications as electrode materials for lithium-ion batteries and electrochem. capacitors, and efficient electrocatalysts for the oxygen redn. reaction in metal-air batteries and fuel cells.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Binary metal oxides have been regarded as ideal and potential anode materials, which can ameliorate and offset the electrochem. performance of the single metal oxides, such as reversible capacity, structural stability and electronic cond.  In this work, monodisperse NiCo2O4 mesoporous microspheres are fabricated by a facile solvothermal method followed by pyrolysis of the Ni0.33Co0.67CO3 precursor.  The Brunauer-Emmett-Teller surface area of NiCo2O4 mesoporous microspheres is detd. to be about 40.58 m2 g-1 with dominant pore diam. of 14.5 nm and narrow size distribution of 10-20 nm.  Our as-prepd. NiCo2O4 products were evaluated as the anode material for the lithium-ion battery application.  It is demonstrated that the special structural features of the NiCo2O4 microspheres including uniformity of the surface texture, the integrity and porosity exert significant effect on the electrochem. performances.  The discharge capacity of NiCo2O4 microspheres could reach 1198 mA h g-1 after 30 discharge-charge cycles at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1.  More importantly, when the c.d. increased to 800 mA·g-1, it can render reversible capacity of 705 mA h g-1 even after 500 cycles, indicating its potential applications for next-generation high power lithium-ion batteries.  The superior battery performance is mainly attributed to the unique micro/nanostructure composed of interconnected NiCo2O4 nanocrystals, which provides good electrolyte diffusion and large electrode-electrolyte contact area, and meanwhile reduces vol. change during charge/discharge process.  The strategy is simple but very effective, and because of its versatility, it could be extended to other high-capacity metal oxide anode materials for lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGozxBuRilGL2rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhcnLiBDraBWw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXoslOitg%253D%253D&amp;md5=2f1ae4ebb15717931c9b659dc9c906ba</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref21" class="rightTabRefNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit21" data-doi="10.1021/cm025556v"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Alcántara, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jaraba, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lavela, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tirado, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NiCo<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub> Spinel: First Report on a Transition Metal Oxide for the Negative Electrode of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The use of NiCo2O4 spinel as anode material in sodium and sodium-ion batteries is examd.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Confined and unconfined SnO2 nanoparticles in the pores of mesoporous carbon were prepd. and tested as anode materials vs. Na.  Both composites present small cryst. SnO2 particles (∼3 nm) but different location and dispersion in the carbon matrix.  When the particles are homogeneously distributed and confined in the carbon pores, an initial reversible capacity of 780 mA h g-1 is achieved with unprecedented capacity retention of 80 and 54% after 100 and 4000 cycles, resp., at a high current rate (50 C, 1800 mA g-1).  Unexpectedly, over two current rate variation cycles from 1 C to 500 C, the composite recovers 81% and 97%, resp. after returning from the 500 C to the 1 C rate.  To our knowledge, no other material with such a long cycling life and superior performance in terms of capacity and rate capability has been reported so far for sodium ion batteries.  HRTEM, XRD, N2 adsorption, XPS and galvanostatic cycling results suggest that confined SnO2 particles undergo an enhanced sodium alloying/dealloying process due to their special confinement inside the pores, which increases their cond., facilitates the diffusion of Na+ ions and buffers the large volumetric changes during charge/discharge.  These high performances cannot be delivered when SnO2 is not confined and not well dispersed in the carbon pores.  This work demonstrates that nano-confinement of anode species in carbon is a valuable concept affording the modification of the fundamental properties of guest species along with their electrochem. performances leading to highly stable and performing materials with a long life for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpmSgtWPTSt8LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liUZNRy7fgPrQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXnsFGgur4%253D&amp;md5=219ee2777f1e53956a82fdbab173128f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref24" class="rightTabRefNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit24" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2012.01.123"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wen, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jin, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Composite of Sulfur and Polypyrrole-Multi Walled Carbon Combinatorial Nanotube as Cathode for Li/S Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In recent years, the design and morphol. control of crystals with tailored facets have become hot spots in the field of electrochem. energy storage devices.  For electrode materials, morphologies play important roles in their activities because their shapes det. how many facets of specific orientation are exposed and therefore available for surface reactions.  This review focuses on the strategies for crystal facet control and the unusual electrochem. properties of electrode materials bound by tailored facets.  Here, electrode materials with tailored facets include transition metal oxides such as SnO2, Co3O4, NiO, Cu2O, and MnO2, elementary substances such as Si and Au, and intercalation compds. such as Li4Ti5O12, LiCoO2, LiMn2O4, LiFePO4, and Na0.7MnO2 for various applications of Li-ion batteries, aq. rechargeable lithium batteries, Na-ion batteries, Li-O2 batteries and supercapacitors.  How these electrode materials with tailored facets affect their electrochem. properties is discussed.  Finally, research opportunities as well as the challenges in this emerging research frontier are highlighted.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpnBkbw2Qn6CbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liUZNRy7fgPrQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkvFCktw%253D%253D&amp;md5=b04efeb748b54942101659b45d042615</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1016/j.matlet.2014.07.170"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fan, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ma, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Miao, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In-Situ Synthesis of Core/Shell Structured Polypyrrole/Hydroquinone Nano-Beads and Electrochemical Capacitance Investigations</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Mater.
