Mater.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">25</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">4646</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">4652</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.201301906</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fe-Doped MnxOy with Hierarchical Porosity as a High-performance Lithium-ion Battery Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ma, Yue; Fang, Chunliu; Ding, Bo; Ji, Ge; Lee, Jim Yang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">33</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4646-4652</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We reported an alternative approach to designing and constructing 3-D manganese oxides with mixed-conducting properties.  Fe-doped MnxOy with connected macropores and mesopores to provide a hierarchical porosity was produced by a facile and scalable nanocasting technique followed by controlled calcination, using a novel macroporous amine-functionalized bromomethylated poly(2,6-dimethyl-1,4-phenylene oxide) (BPPO) membrane as the sacrificial template.  The macropores in the final product were mainly formed by the reverse-replication of the membrane porous structure, and interconnected via branches in the pore system.  The macropores cushioned the vol. change in the conversion reaction during cycling, and also acted as reservoirs and thoroughfares to improve Li+ transport in the electrolyte phase.  The mesopores between nanocryst. primary particles were formed upon heat treatment; and provided the large interfacial contact between electrolyte and electrode material to support a high Li+ flux across the solid/liq. interface.  The selection of iron as a dopant was intentional: The redox potential of iron (1.0 V for discharge/1.7 V for charge) is higher than that of manganese (0.5 V for discharge/1.2 V for charge).  Hence, the evenly distributed iron could remain in the zero valent state during a large part of MnxOy conversion reaction, serving conceptually the dual function of 1) elec. wiring of the electroactive material to lower the resistance to electron transport and 2) promoting ionic conduction by creating narrowly spaced interfaces at the oxide grain boundary.  Electrochem. measurements showed that the Fe-doped MnxOy composite had the best overall performance: a large reversible capacity of 620 mA.h.g-1 for 100 cycles at the c.d. of 200 mA.g-1, good rate capability up to 1600 mA.g-1 and outstanding cycle life even at very high c.d. (900 cycles at 1500 mA.g-1).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Exploring highly-efficient and low-cost bifunctional electrocatalysts for both oxygen redn. reaction (ORR) and oxygen evolution reactions (OER) in the renewable energy area has gained momentum but still remains a significant challenge. The improved electrochem. performance is considered due to the mesoporous nature of the products, the addn. of 3DGNs, 3D assembled hierarchical architecture and decrease in vol. expansion during cycling.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The growth of three-dimensional (3D) porous NiCo2O4 nanowire arrays on a carbon fiber cloth (denoted as NCO@CFC) via a facile low-cost soln. method combined with a subsequent annealing treatment is reported.  The structure and morphol. of the materials were characterized by X-ray diffraction, field-emission SEM, and transmission electron microscopy.  Owing to the unique 3D hierarchical architecture, the NCO@CFC nanowires as a flexible electrode material for lithium-ion batteries exhibit a stable cycling performance (92.3% retention after 100 cycles), a fairly high rate capacity (507 mA h/g at 4000 mA/g), and an enhanced lithium storage capacity.  When employed as an electrode material for sodium-ion batteries, the NCO@CFC is investigated in comparison with a 3D ordered array structure and exhibits similar charge/discharge characteristics and a feasible electrochem. performance.  The greatly improved electrochem. performance could be ascribed to the 3D porous nanostructure of the NCO@CFC nanowire arrays together with a novel carbon skeleton, which provides enough space to allow vol. expansion during the Li+/Na+ insertion/extn. process and facilitates rapid transport of ions and electrons.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoXw_-7XiLxqbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgVrUM_oO-D2w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlajur%252FJ&amp;md5=8e7a91a2db1c011f15c3343d388e3988</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref42" class="rightTabRefNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit42" data-doi="10.1039/c3ra23466e"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hou, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrode Materials for Aqueous Asymmetric Supercapacitors</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">RSC Adv.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">3</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">13059</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">13084</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  An asym. supercapacitor (ASC) is a supercapacitor based on two different electrode materials.  One electrode is based on redox (Faradic) reactions with or without non-faradaic reactions, and the other one is mostly based on elec. double-layer (non-Faradic or electrostatic) absorption/desportion.  Aq. electrolytes have higher ionic cond., larger capacitance and better safety than the org. electrolytes.  Herein, some key electrode materials for aq. ASCs are primarily reviewed, which provide a new direction for power sources to have higher energy d. at high power densities, compared with traditional capacitors.  Their neg. electrode materials include carbonaceous materials (porous carbons, carbon nanotubes and graphene), oxides (V2O5 and MoO3) and their composites, and their pos. electrode materials include carbonaceous materials, oxides (RuO2, MnO2, MoO3, V2O5, PbO2, Co3O4), Ni(OH)2, intercalation compds. (LiCoO2, LiMn2O4, Li[NiCoMn]1/3O2, NaMnO2 and KMnO2).  We describe the latest work on these electrode materials, and a particular focus is directed to the fabrication and electrochem. performance of various nanostructured electrode materials and some assembled ASCs.  Finally, the future trends and prospects on advanced energy storage materials are suggested.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpQJfcktMTcw7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgVrUM_oO-D2w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFeqtr3O&amp;md5=512cd93a2cde72e85beda226e109d32b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref43" class="rightTabRefNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit43" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA01398H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Conductive Polymer Coated MoO<sub>3</sub> Anode Enables an Al-Ion Capacitor with High Performance</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. capacitors are becoming promising energy conversion/storage and power output devices.  However, high cost and low energy d. are two serious disadvantages.  By integrating the advantages of Li-/Na-ion batteries and electrochem. capacitors, Li-/Na-ion capacitors have been explored recently.  Al is very cheap and is the most abundant metal element on the earth.  There are few reports on Al-ion capacitors due to the challenges in finding a suitable anode with large capacitance and good rate performance.  Here, the feasibility of assembling an Al-ion capacitor with good electrochem. performance is demonstrated.  The Al-ion capacitor is assembled by using a composite of MoO3 nanotubes coated by a conductive polypyrrole (PPy@MoO3) as an anode, which functions via a redox intercalation/deintercalation of Al3+ ions in aq. soln.  It delivers a capacitance of 693 F/g, about 3 times higher than that of electrode materials for sodium-ion capacitors in aq. soln.  Combined with an activated carbon (AC) cathode, the Al-ion capacitor presents an energy d. of 30 W h/kg and an excellent cycling life with 93% capacitance retention after 1800 cycles.  This finding provides another energy storage device with low cost and promotes the application of capacitors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr-B8WDSiffkbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgVrUM_oO-D2w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XjsVGlsLw%253D&amp;md5=7c98fb2f66d51d6f363b28d504efb300</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref44" class="rightTabRefNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit44" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2012.09.100"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Holze, R.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polypyrrole-Coated LiV<sub>3</sub>O<sub>8</sub>-Nanocomposites with Good Electrochemical Performance as Anode Material for Aqueous Rechargeable Lithium Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. TEM coupled with energy dispersive X-ray spectrometry (EDX) indicates that the Co(Ni)/Mo ratio inside crystallites changes without any modification over MoS2 layers (size and stacking). Fe 2p3/2 spectra from high-spin compds.  The multiplets fit most spectra well, particularly when contributions attributed to surface peaks and shake-up satellites were included.  This information was useful for fitting of the complex Fe 2p3/2 spectra for Fe3O4 where both Fe2+ and Fe3+ species are present.  As the ionic bond character of the Fe-ligand bond increased, the binding energy assocd. with either the ferrous or ferric 2p3/2 photoelectron peak increased.  This is due to the decrease in shielding of the Fe cation by the more increasingly electroneg. ligands.  Also the difference in energy between a high-spin Fe 2p3/2 peak and its corresponding shake-up satellite peak increased as the electronegativity of the ligand increased.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Magnetic nest-like γ-Fe2O3/ZnO double-shelled hollow nanostructures have been successfully synthesized via a multi-step process.  The materials have been thoroughly characterized by different techniques.  These interesting nest-like hollow nanostructures are composed of ZnO nanoflakes grown on the surface of γ-Fe2O3 hollow spheres.  Importantly, these magnetic hollow nanostructures show very high visible-light photocatalytic activity for the degrdn. of different org. dyes including methylene blue (MB), Rhodamine-B (RhB), and methyl orange (MO).  It is further demonstrated that these γ-Fe2O3/ZnO hybrid photocatalysts are highly stable and can be used repeatedly.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpd89c6pR6DQbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liJ4o3mcM6xHQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhsF2qsrbI&amp;md5=935b8ed2a0c4e4831da744158cc697bb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref54" class="rightTabRefNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit54" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.09.002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yan, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qin, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pan, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MgFe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub>/Reduced Graphene Oxide Composites as High-Performance Anode Materials for Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim. Acta</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">180</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">616</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">621</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2015.09.002</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MgFe2O4/reduced graphene oxide composites as high-performance anode materials for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Xiaojie; Chen, Taiqiang; Yan, Dong; Qin, Wei; Hu, Bingwen; Sun, Zhuo; Pan, Likun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">180</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">616-621</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MgFe2O4/reduced graphene oxide composites (MFO/RGO) were prepd. via a facile microwave assisted redn. of graphene oxide in MFO precursor soln., and used as anode materials for sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  Their morphol., structure and electrochem. performance were characterized by field emission SEM, transmission electron microscopy, X-ray diffraction, nitrogen adsorption-desorption isotherms, galvanostatic charge/discharge tests, cyclic voltammetry and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy, resp.  The results show that MFO/RGO composite with 20 wt.% RGO exhibits a max. reversible capacity of about 347.5 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 after 70 cycles with good cycling stability.  The excellent electrochem. performance of MFO/RGO composites should be attributed to the synergistic effect of MFO and RGO to form a porous conductive network structure which offers the increased sp. surface area, the facilitated electron transfer ability and the effective buffering of vol. expansion.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr_dCg6DUiuhLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liJ4o3mcM6xHQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVyjur3O&amp;md5=cb73bb0af3e1223d28e31908bb466d0e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref55" class="rightTabRefNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit55" data-doi="10.1021/am400497v"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Teh, P. F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pramana, S. S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sharma, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ko, Y. W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Madhavi, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrospun Zn<sub>1–x</sub>Mn<sub>x</sub>Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub> Nanofibers as Anodes for Lithium-Ion Batteries and the Impact of Mixed Transition Metallic Oxides on Battery Performance</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">5461</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">5467</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/am400497v</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i14">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.7b12503" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.7b12503</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">SEM images of PPy-NTs; TEM images of PPy-NTs and CFO-PPy-NTs at low magnification; SEM image of CoFe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub> nanoparticles; comparison between the XRD patterns of CFO-NPs and CFO-PPy-NTs; XRD pattern of PPy-NTs; high-resolution XPS spectra of PPy-NTs including C 1s and N 1s; pore size distribution of PPy-NTs; BJH adsorption–desorption cumulative pore volumes of PPy-NTs and CFO-PPy-NTs; CV scan curves of the CFO-PPy-NTs; the equivalent circuit for the EIS analysis; high-resolution XPS spectra of Co 2p and Fe 2p of the cycled CFO-PPy-NTs; SEM images of pristine electrode of CFO-PPy-NTs; SEM images of pristine electrode of CoFe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub> nanoparticles (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b12503/suppl_file/am7b12503_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b12503/suppl_file/am7b12503_si_001.pdf">am7b12503_si_001.pdf (12.25 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="90f6e9957db7775c-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e9957db7775c-SJC">
"use strict"
//Script checks gdpr cookie and submits form
	/* 
	Create an in-page pop-up message, only for the InfoCentral homepage, that will gather email registrants for the library marketing list.
	 
	Needs the end point
	*/

var infoCentralCapture = (function() {

    //Detect mobile device
    window.mobilecheck = function() {
        var check = false;
        (function(a){if(/(android|bb\d+|meego).+mobile|avantgo|bada\/|blackberry|blazer|compal|elaine|fennec|hiptop|iemobile|ip(hone|od)|iris|kindle|lge |maemo|midp|mmp|mobile.+firefox|netfront|opera wa|abac|ac(er|oo|s\-)|ai(ko|rn)|al(av|ca|co)|amoi|an(ex|ny|yw)|aptu|ar(ch|go)|as(te|us)|attw|au(di|\-m|r |s )|avan|be(ck|ll|nq)|bi(lb|rd)|bl(ac|az)|br(e|v)w|bumb|bw\-(n|u)|c55\/|capi|ccwa|cdm\-|cell|chtm|cldc|cmd\-|co(mp|nd)|craw|da(it|ll|ng)|dbte|dc\-s|devi|dica|dmob|do(c|p)o|ds(12|\-d)|el(49|ai)|em(l2|ul)|er(ic|k0)|esl8|ez([4-7]0|os|wa|ze)|fetc|fly(\-|_)|g1 u|g560|gene|gf\-5|g\-mo|go(\.w|od)|gr(ad|un)|haie|hcit|hd\-(m|p|t)|hei\-|hi(pt|ta)|hp( i|ip)|hs\-c|ht(c(\-| |_|a|g|p|s|t)|tp)|hu(aw|tc)|i\-(20|go|ma)|i230|iac( |\-|\/)|ibro|idea|ig01|ikom|im1k|inno|ipaq|iris|ja(t|v)a|jbro|jemu|jigs|kddi|keji|kgt( |\/)|klon|kpt |kwc\-|kyo(c|k)|le(no|xi)|lg( g|\/(k|l|u)|50|54|\-[a-w])|libw|lynx|m1\-w|m3ga|m50\/|ma(te|ui|xo)|mc(01|21|ca)|m\-cr|me(rc|ri)|mi(o8|oa|ts)|mmef|mo(01|02|bi|de|do|t(\-| |o|v)|zz)|mt(50|p1|v )|mwbp|mywa|n10[0-2]|n20[2-3]|n30(0|2)|n50(0|2|5)|n7(0(0|1)|10)|ne((c|m)\-|on|tf|wf|wg|wt)|nok(6|i)|nzph|o2im|op(ti|wv)|oran|owg1|p800|pan(a|d|t)|pdxg|pg(13|\-([1-8]|c))|phil|pire|pl(ay|uc)|pn\-2|po(ck|rt|se)|prox|psio|pt\-g|qa\-a|qc(07|12|21|32|60|\-[2-7]|i\-)|qtek|r380|r600|raks|rim9|ro(ve|zo)|s55\/|sa(ge|ma|mm|ms|ny|va)|sc(01|h\-|oo|p\-)|sdk\/|se(c(\-|0|1)|47|mc|nd|ri)|sgh\-|shar|sie(\-|m)|sk\-0|sl(45|id)|sm(al|ar|b3|it|t5)|so(ft|ny)|sp(01|h\-|v\-|v )|sy(01|mb)|t2(18|50)|t6(00|10|18)|ta(gt|lk)|tcl\-|tdg\-|tel(i|m)|tim\-|t\-mo|to(pl|sh)|ts(70|m\-|m3|m5)|tx\-9|up(\.b|g1|si)|utst|v400|v750|veri|vi(rg|te)|vk(40|5[0-3]|\-v)|vm40|voda|vulc|vx(52|53|60|61|70|80|81|83|85|98)|w3c(\-| )|webc|whit|wi(g |nc|nw)|wmlb|wonu|x700|yas\-|your|zeto|zte\-/i.test(a.substr(0,4))) check = true;})(navigator.userAgent||navigator.vendor||window.opera);
              return check;
        };

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').addClass('mobile');
    }

    var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>


                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="90f6e9957db7775c-SJC">
var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>
